────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Studio scale Probe droid build.

E=MC2...nobody buddy, its long OOP, was released by Steve Neisen a while back, mastered by our own Rolando Guiterrez.

Stu.... yeah would be one hell of a project, i thought about it, but i wanted my Probe Droid NOW....'cos im a spoilt lil' brat :lol.

Quincy.... yes buddy, M16 is used a lot on this model, ive only scratched the surface...its kinda weird, not that many kits are on the PD so far, it seems they just used lots of parts, from the few kits they used....donor wise, its not too spendy....nowhere near the ATST.

Simon...yeah you shoulda lol, the SMT is a nice little kit though, but i just cant build anything nowadays, that isnt studio scale and i LOVE the Probe droid.

JP... yes, getting one on the third party market, is a big cost, i had to really ponder it, couple that with the kits i want to burn up on it, yeah.....kinda crazy...but then...who said we studio guys were sane people anyways :lol.

Hoping to get a little more done today, waiting on a few parts, but i think i can just about finish off the top hat, and get to drilling out the smaller eyeballs to fit new larger Plastruct lamps.

bests......lee

Re: Studio scale Probe droid build.

One more gig & I'm free till mid Jan, so there will be some PD time coming up mate. That little tube seems really odd & random, I'm sure I've seen a better pic of it & it has some detail to it somewhere. I have all my Ref on my old computer so will dig it out & see what PD stuff I have. With the tube sat on the plate I assumed it was a kit part.

ILM did some weird stuff at times. One thing I'm going to try and do is scribe under the top part of the dome ( the part you just levelled) to make it look like a separate piece.

All the plating is pretty flush to the head but the top part is clearly separated. I think this would make a huge difference to the final look & just take it one step closer to looking authentic.

Been trying to find black marbles for the small eye lenses also, What s the diameter of the hole in the lamp shades?

Post #77  (forum post #1481401)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Dec 17, 2010 at 6:31 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Studio scale Probe droid build.

moffeaton said:

			Thanks, Guy!
		

Click to expand...

No problem Jason, hope they can help in some way?

I do have to say though I only had 30 mins to sneak out of the show in Sydney & run down to the exhibition. The photos where more about the actual colour of the prop than detail as you know painting this thing is a challenge & a half. I wanted to try & capture the colour you see under studio lighting with the naked eye & without any flash, some of the shots are with no flash & all different exposures to capture the closest look that we see with our eyes. 

Still bloody difficult with no tripod & limited time but I know what to do next time when I paint it again & which shot is the best example of the true colour of the PD.

This said its still all pointless as what we see is all effected by the choice of lighting as its displayed & as you look at it it doesn't really show any sign of the brown even up close, its a bit of a paint crime scene & does take some forensic's to work it out with out seeing it in the flesh:lol

I did have another 100 shots of this & the sand crawler from my return the next day, but they mysteriously vanished from my laptop after (cough Cough) my girlfriend spent a day doing work on it. It was only a few months later I realised I'd lost over 500 shots taken at the exhibition :cry

I think I also found a red/orange marking that I hadn't noticed before on other ref or on private builds, so well worth the hassle getting there, I think the staff thought I was some serious weirdo, Panting out of breath whilst taking pics of star wars model's :cool

Re: Studio scale Probe droid build.

That's normal Guy.

On this pic, the outer circle is clearly visible : 

[IMAGE: Tophatpart.png]

Actually that's the back of a part that's not intented to be seen, there are 6 parts in the kits and those ejection marks are uneven from part to part ! Add to that the very close up and the lightning when I took the pic (the pins was not visible when I took a pic with flash), when you see it in the flesh you can barely see the outer circle ! And with a coat of primer and paint it would be almost invisible !

Since you have the kit, just check your part and you'll that's the correct part.

Post #277  (forum post #1545700)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Feb 7, 2011 at 12:26 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Made a start on the chest box finally. I know why i put it off now lol. This is the third one i cut.

One huge factor, is the fact the NiceN kit body, differs in angle to the prop, the prop, seems a much more steep "conical" shape.

This normally, would not be a problem, until you have to stuff a Morser Karl cannon inside said box and require it to stand off this angle, at a near dead 90 degree's....then, its gets a little frustrating.

Ive managed to build, what im calling a happy medium now, even the size (width/height) is affected by the body being a bit off TBH, kit parts, never lie i guess :lol.

Ive taped it on for now, so i can show you guys, i know its NOT spot on, sadly, it never will be using the kit body, but, what ye reckon thus far oh counters of the rivet :lol?

bests......lee

Post #287  (forum post #1556918)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Feb 15, 2011 at 8:51 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Scott, the cone shapes, hmm Moe said they were Plastruct lamps on the mid section joints, but im not so sure, they look more like F1 rims with the tops cut off, i still need to look into it further.

The lower joints are Plastruct lamps for sure, in fact the legs themselves are Plastruct rectangular tubing, hollow, and that kinda why laser cutting and alloy legs, wont work on this model, it would be overkill, Moe sent me the sizes the other day, and they arrived this AM....woot!

The joints themselves, look very frail, its just two strips of styrene to hold the joint on, and a bolt through the centre, not sure if ill be articulating them, but them more i think about it, them more i may as well go through that fuss, as it would be worth it, to have movable legs i guess.

Thanks Kevin

Post #289  (forum post #1563109)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Feb 19, 2011 at 4:15 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I did all my Red 4 engine pulls with Alumilite so it's doable (now I would prefer another kind of resin, slow-setting), but the Saturn parts have no details (beside the raised lines) so you can do it easily with Aluminite in a 2-parts mold. With some baby powder you won't have any airbubble ! As for the rubber, it's up to you, maybe you can get the Alumilite set (rubber, resin and release agent) ? You would have enough rubber to mold those parts and more ! Alumilite is not cheap though but it can be worth it if you dont plan to mold/cast more parts for other projets or largest parts. If you do, prefer to buy another brand of resin.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #291  (forum post #1564018)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Feb 20, 2011 at 1:02 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ralphee said:

			Julien thank you for that, ill give the Alumilite a go. Going to just cast the smaller joints now, seeing as i have enough Saturns spare for the larger joints.

I think ill be OK with just an open mold for the small ones?

lee
		

Click to expand...

 

Yeah an open mold sounds good for those small parts, once the back sanded flat they will do the job perfectly and it will be easier for you to spot any airbubbles ! For such parts, Alumilite is perfect and you wont waste too much time to get them cured, just be very careful to mix parts A and B very well (I found that's more important than with other resin) because you can easily get some uncured places on your parts. I had a lot when I did my first castings. 

I'm not the best caster but if you need any help/advice let me know !

Post #293  (forum post #1564772)
Author    : tk1608
Date      : Feb 21, 2011 at 5:32 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey Lee, sorry just seen this...I think I'm too late if you've already sent for it, but anyhoo..

I got from tiranti, Resin "Biresin G26 N "...it's a 50-50 mix, so easy to do..dries to the usual yellowy colour. It's starts to set up fairly fast,..a minute or two, I'm wondering if it's a large part, you might need a slower setting time to give you time to work the bubbles out..

And Rubber "Addition Cure 33"...again it's a 50-50 mix, no messing about with weighing the stuff, and tiny amounts of catalist. I've had trouble with it not curing before so this stuff is great for me ..when I mix the rubber I got a lot of bubbles in the mixture and I was worried about that, but when it's set they seem to have risen away from the parts, so it turned out OK...and it dries clear.   They're both about £30 per kit plus P&P..

Also I've found that some mould release wax in there, makes the resin flow a bit better, as well as making it easier to get the parts out of course..
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Cheers

Phil

Post #298  (forum post #1571882)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Feb 26, 2011 at 12:33 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hah, Guy, sorry buddy, not much excitement im afraid, plans went a little south on the leg struts today, decided to try get better casts outta this Alumilite.

First runs were pretty poor, i think id over powdered the mold TBH, and i was just plain pouring from the corner, this was not letting the resin settle well, and giving some really awful air bubbles.

Sooo, i sat and tried to correct my mistakes, tried less powder, just a light brushing, then, once i poured the resin, i swirled the mold a little. 

This worked out far better, still some small bubbles, but nothing like i was getting first time out the gate.

Anyhoo, ive got your large Saturn parts done, and im working on the smaller joints now, i KNOW these arent great guys, its my first time trying this, just wish i had a slower resin, but i think, thus far, these parts are usable, dont look too bad i guess.

Good news is, the molds are as tougher than Juan Manuel Marquez, so i think ill get a lot of pulls from them.

Tomorrow, i have permission from her Majesty to start a leg off, so im hoping i can get a good bit done Sunday, so ill have a better update for you Guy lol.

lee

Post #300  (forum post #1571994)
Author    : marvin
Date      : Feb 26, 2011 at 2:07 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Lee,

Those cast look pretty good! I usually pour in a scoop of baby powder, swirl it around and ditch the exces powder. You can simply blow into the mold hard so there's no real white buildup anymore or it a spot is hard to reach: use your airbrush!

I swirl a bit of resin around in the mold and move around and bust all airbubbles with a toothpick before pouring the rest of the resin. With an open mold like this you should be able to get bubble free surfaces. 

So what now? Are you hooked on casting now that you've tried it?!?

Marvin
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #305  (forum post #1572450)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Feb 26, 2011 at 11:02 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Guy, i did try the fridge, seemed ok, but, swirling the resin at the pour, seemed to work things out a little better.

This stuff really does go off fast, the chemical reaction is pretty instant after pouring, so you have to have just get on with it.

TBH, id like maybe another 5 maybe ten mins work time, make sure ALL air is pulled out.

Jason, thanks man, ill get there, its a steep learning curve this casting lark, so weird silly things like talc application, and mold swirling make such critical changes to the cast.

James, its Alumilite Super Plastic resin, with the accompanying rubber. If you want to try it, great, its not too bad, easy to mix etc etc, but id go a different route now from Tiranti's range here in the UK.

I will say the Alumilite rubber seems pretty hardy though, ive not a tear or pull yet, think its a pretty high shore rating though?

lee

Post #349  (forum post #1593302)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Mar 14, 2011 at 9:22 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well, had all these plans to finish one of these this weekend, but, best laid plans huh lol.

Anyhoo, here is the first articulating leg. I used Plastruct tube, as close to the correct size as poss (havent got a lathe so could turn them sadly)  cut it to size and filled it with resin.

I drilled out the centre to accept a 4/40 bolt, and bingo. Lining up the adjacent Saturn V parts was a ***** though, its VERY tricky doing all this by hand/sanding, and getting it to run true, but, within a mm or so, its straight as can be....so im happy about that lol.

Works very well though, with only the lightest of pressure to make the pinch hold, and, still allow movement. They weigh nothing really.

A few kit parts are added here just so i could scale it up as close as poss.

From here, ill now plan...LOL to finish up this coming weekend, by making the top Saturn V joint articulate, and, add the rest of the kit parts that are known.

Oh, and i had to use 4/40 countersunk in the pics, as i had no cap heads, that are used on the prop, need to get some ordered. They tap into the resin joint perfectly though.

lee

Well, my feeble amount of time at the bench got the pincer and some donors added.

All works perfectly too. Ive tried to emulate how ILM's joints/pincers worked as best i can.

The top Saturn V joint is also now ready for action, i just cut two tabs in styrene, glued internally, and an axle in the centre, this axle will snap into the opposing half via a magnet.

A few more parts to add, few more to find, and finish off the top joint to body bracket, and this leg is done. Really fun to have it all articulate though, should be cool when completed to mess around a little, while making Probe droid noises :lol

Thanks Andre.

Well again, weekend didnt offer me much time, but i managed to cut most of the other tubing for the rest of the legs, and, get this first leg fitted.

Im very limited in how to attach the leg, and have it rotate in the body with this kit, best option would have been a bolt through the lower body, but, seeing as this is a one piece deal.......

So i used magnets and a small metal washer......not 100% cannon, but it works perfectly, very solid fit, and removable...bonus.

Hoping i can get to motor on now and get this thing ready for paint come the warmer months, plan is to finish it up for the summer.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Took a few pics of the progress today for Guy. First leg now finished, and a part missing from the current props pincer added, Chronicles aided this find, damper will be added after painting.

Started out on the second Saturn V leg joint, bit trickier this one, three cuts needed on the can to form the joint, so i used my drill press, and a cutting disc to pull it off, went well.

Added styrene tabs as a guide for rotation, and the whole deal will again snap together with magnets.

Should have a big portion of this leg wrapped up come Monday, then it gets a bit easier.

bests......lee

Post #416  (forum post #1646495)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Apr 21, 2011 at 4:47 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hmm mixed results...

The Saturn v Knuckle has come out great & the first 3 pulls only have 2 bubbles between them & are more than usable.

The Saturn V- M16 part is a different matter. The mould had some air bubbles around the undercut sections, I'd even blocked it off at the back to help this but the pulls had loads of bubbles round the detail & due to the undercuts it was near impossible to remove the pull without tearing the mould. The 3rd attempt destroyed the mould.

However If I hack out the M16 part of the pull I can still use the outer ring with original M16 parts on the inside, I will try to cast theM16 wheel again but on its own this time to see if its any better. 

Pics to follow
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #417  (forum post #1646718)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Apr 21, 2011 at 8:45 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Guy

Well not a total loss then. Just so you know, the M3 Halftrack does use the same drivetrain as the M16 buddy, not sure if that will save you casting them?

As for the Saturn V small knuckle, i drilled a 2.4mm hole in the back cone, for a 4/40 cap head to pass through, not sure how ILM did there joint with no visible screw, but some do have a larger hole.....so maybe the bolt is inside the hollow original part?

The way ive done it, you can really notice, as the cap head, is captive by a 4mm hole, in the back on said, cast cone...allowing me to drill just a 2.5mm hole for access.........if that makes sense?

lee

Not that far from done on this now. Its been a niggly leg to build, joints were a pain to allign, but turned out pretty good, all seems very true and straight, and it all functions very well.

The pincer joint, i think "should" be Plastruct LF parts, but TBH, i see a ridge on them at the base....making me think thats the wrong part..so i went for Tyrrell rims trimmed down a bit, seems closer to my eye anyway.....others mileage may vary :lol.

Few pics for Guy to show the knuckle progression, hope that helps a little buddy.

Now a few donors to add, and a VERY tricky pincer to build, and i can wrap this one up.

Julien the plating is a bit of a confusing one......id say they may heated styrene, and pushed it in to warp into the Saturn V? Very weird this prop, even that pinch running around the head confuses me, were they found items/domes glued together, or an elaborate vacform......baffled, and sadly, so little info of the build in any publications.

I know they build two sets of legs, the proto legs are soooo different to the final model ILM used...Rolando based his kit on the first draft of legs, which are the same......but very different......if you get my drift lol.

Post #527  (forum post #1677074)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : May 13, 2011 at 11:55 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Slowly getting there,

Just need to make one more leg section & the knuckles for 3 legs & claws before the Damper work starts....few!!

[IMAGE: PDBUM.jpg]

For the larger leg mounts I kinda rushed it a bit. They look neat but aren't as stable as Lees as I didn't add a support tube inside but the Large steel washers have the correct Pin hole in them & aare sunk into the body, then neatened up with Apoxie sculpt so its all flush. I also replaced the resin screws for real ones so I could recess them.

The smaller legs where a lot easier to do, I drilled a 9.5mm hole in the body & hammered 10mm Deep countersunk magnets into the hole, they're in tight as dandy and flush as hell, the Pins are a perfect fit so the magnets act as support tube also, they're also invisible(give or take a mm here & there). :cool
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #561  (forum post #1689613)
Author    : dragnink
Date      : May 23, 2011 at 2:51 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Guy, when I was playing around ages ago I'd shoot each frame then batch import into windows movie maker.. I think the mac-type equivalent for simple stuff would be FrameByFrame? Final Cut Pro/Express should let you do consecutive frame editing too. If you want to go more serious and have a decent camera that you can go manual with so you don't get exposure/light flickr you can go with something like Dragon Stop Motion which is really good for mac and pc alike, pairs up well to the Canon/Nikon SLR's that have live view. Phil Tippett has been having some fun with a setup like that lately I heard...

			Does anyone know of a frame by frame App for Mac to do stop mo with. If I set up my tri pod & take snaps can you put it into a movie App and make mini Movies???

Cheers Lee, Naaaa I bottled it, its in with the stuff I sent to you today, be carful though as its in the packing on the box, you'll suss it when you get it, I didn't want to re open the packet so put it in another and attached it to the first :eek

I managed to put an offer on a Hood on ebay for £14 and they bit so got it at a good price.

I re made the damper mount that you sent from scratch as it was a little too big for my rods, after an age of Pissssing around trying to round them I cme up with a cunning plan!!!! I cut some styrene tube in half, then glued 400 wet n dry inside one of the halves....Just ran the Damper mount up and down

inside the tube and it worked a treat and took about 30 sec's...after wasting most of the afternoon :lol. I also made the Leg mount from the T strip and put that in the mold today also so I don't have to keep making them. No More Rubber left so lets hope they come out as nice as yours.

I'm determined to get legs one & 2 damperd up tomorrow if its the last thing I do :love

Cheers Lee, It was a faff at first but once you've done one, you get what not to do and what works best. My biggest hassle was drilling the styrene supports, they kept splitting apart. They're made of .060 x .186 strip with a .080 x .186 for the middle section, so they're not quite square.

They work like butter, I can get each leg just shy of straight & 90 degrees if not more, only one of the pins is et in place so I'll remove em to prime. On the 10/4 leg the brass rod hits the knuckle before it goes in the straight position, theres no way around this though with out changing the design.

The U(Kit Part) channel is for the leg with the Karl Lamps, It def tapers down from the knuckle to the karl part, on the pics it looks like a barrel but its just full of glue. Will have a look in the M16 now but I have checked it already, fingers crossed
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Need some pointers on snow though guys, i have the Scenic model snow gear, but, it seems a bit brutal, wanted to go for a more "dusted" look.

Ive heard of baby powder being used on Railroads, anybody tried it? Really need it to look dusted, not a big mucky splat of white, so to speak.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #607  (forum post #1715437)
Author    : qcfoundry
Date      : Jun 10, 2011 at 8:26 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Lee,

For my chicken i've bumped out a lot of swatches for snow and its all about scale.  For something along the chicken scale, nothing is as good as microballoons -- it sifts and falls like sand (f'n brilliant). For something larger like your PD, you may actually see the jagged edges of snow flakes and might try the hobby store products (woodland scenics, deluxe, or hudson/allen).  I wouldn't touch baby powder or baking powder....i would want to work with trully inert materials.  I'll try to send you pics of my swatches this weekend.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #608  (forum post #1715474)

Post #632  (forum post #1771116)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Jul 17, 2011 at 4:17 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Small update, decided while i zip between the remaining work on the legs, id get experimenting with weathering this thing.

Its really NOT easy, Guy you are so right, its one for sleepless nights lol.

My base color, it now becomes apparent, is a tad too light, no great shakes, this will be fixed with a new trick ive found.

Mixing a 50/50 mix of Dullcote and thinners, to a tiny amount of colored pigment (i used MIG) works wonders, it creates a great transparent filter, rather than a stark coat of paint.

Remember, this still has to look grey to the eye, but with hues and mists that vary from pic to pic, its actually darker than the pics here, i just cant seem to get a good portrayal in the camera damnit lol.

Ive shot a transparent coat of rust on the body here over the TS66 and Neutral grey, not gone too heavy yet, as i said, its all a learning curve for me, but the effect seems to work, just takes time to build it up, and then finally darken it all down with a final black transparent filter, fixing my basecoat glare, and darkening the rust filter.

More to come soon, unless i go insane and end up in the loony bin.

bests.....lee

Mate I used some k&s tube cut to length after jabbing a hole through the foam in the head, made an easy channel to thread the wires through to the centre of the head without catching. You could just drill a hole the same size as the metal tube and paint the tip of the tube to match the PD colour.

Post #682  (forum post #1806185)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Aug 6, 2011 at 11:57 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ha, Lee,   I was just about to give up looking for a pen to fit the ankle joints, been through every draw in the house....tried 30 pens, pencils, everything I could to fit the small ankles........ Then it hit me!

Knitting needle's, they come all sizes and are pretty uniform....... Quick trip to Hobby Craft and voila an 8mm Knitting needle does a perfect job.

I new I'd get there in the end :lol

I think it must be a first to cross studio scale and Knitting? I was hoping they would be hollow as these could make great tubing, sadly they're solid but work really well with knives, saw's, sanding and polishing.

Couldn't resist tonight. This is by no means how the final paint will look. This is all just testing idea's and seeing what works and what doesn't. 

I feel a lot more confident this time around and already after 30 mins have a good Idea how I will paint it. Lots of layers, all acrylic very very thinned paint. I'll go over this with the base coat now as I'll need to start again to fine tune the final results. This was started about 25min ago so I know I can work quick with this as well. 

This is a quick test but opinions would be more than appreciated? Colours used are stock Brown with a few drops of orange and german grey, a tad of black then misted with medium Grey. Its a quick photo with flash so colours aren't as nice here as they are to the eye....well as always daylight will tell a lot more.

Post #728  (forum post #1860124)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Sep 3, 2011 at 2:26 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks mate, I'm chuffed with how its turning out. I'm still not in trouble for painting so thats going well.

I'd thicken the mix when you do inside the recesses, its prone to running in there if its too thin. I'm using oil paint to do the dark streaks (black n white mixed to a dark grey. I've also done some of the gloss patching with red n black and it works a treat. 

I've managed to get each layer thin enough to buff through with just spit n kitchen roll so its getting a nice gloss and patchy effect at the same time. I love it when a plan comes together.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sharing is caring :cool

Doing a build like this is made so much easier when you can bounce ideas off each other. It will be a great day when we see them both finished next to each other, especially after all the effort Lee and I have put into making these 2 PD's

come to life. 

I really hope people follow Lee's lead with the stop mo legs, even for those that have em on display now I really recommend having a go at making new legs.

I still find it amazing to think aside from the ILM model there may only be 2 in the world that have the stop mo legs, it gives it a real sense of History and charm to what would just normally be a very cool looking display. The satisfaction of being able to walk past your PD and tweak the leg position is just so ace.

Post #801  (forum post #1895910)
Author    : STEVE THE SWEDE
Date      : Sep 17, 2011 at 5:05 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Wow, just WOW! Being a huge fan of the probe droid (one of my absolute fav designs) and one who also built this kit way back I'm blown away by the work you guys done! People need to know that this is without doubt one of the toughest garage kits out there to put together. A total nightmare to be frank! The mods you've done are just incredible! I bet non of you have wifes, kids and a day job!?:lol Once again, INCREDIBLE!

When it comes to the paint job of this model it's sure a tough nut to crack! When I built this kit as a commission 4 years ago I remember spending a HUGE amount of time trying to figure it out. IMO, people tend to go way to brown. The state the probe is in today looks completely wrong compared to how it looked in behind the scenes pics from the filming period. I'm whilling to bet that some way down the road the model got re-weathered, possible for ROTJ!? I'm only speculating but could the probe have been planned for a ROTJ apperance? There's at least one promo pic that shows the full scale probe on the death star hangar floor together with TIE pilots. Once again only speculations from my part. IMO, the paint scheme doesn't fit with the weathering style that was used on the ESB models. The ESB stuff was actually rather sloppy when it comes to the weathering department, mostly greys and blacks. It do however fit the ROTJ models more earthy tone weathering style rather good! Compare it to the speeder bike models!

Another thing that seems like a re-weathering could have taken place is the huge black bug eyes on the Saturn bodies. Both in the pre-production photos and the behind the scenes shoots they are gloss. Now they have both been cut back with a satin clear coat. I’m aware though that this could have been done during filming to reduce reflections but I haven’t been able to find a behind the scene pic yet with the satin eyes.

When I painted it I decided to go for a grey slightly metalic look with a hint of brown instead of the other way around. Trust me, I love what you guys are doing but if I may just raise my oppinion (feel free to tell me to go to hell if I’m out of place) I think that you’re both going a bit heavy on the brown coats. Remember that most pics of the probe from the tours are taken with a flash. That tends to bring out top weathering layers thus making it look more brown then it really is. Personally as I said earlier, not even sure this is how it appeared back in 79. PLEASE don’t take this the wrong way, just a thought from one fellow probe nut to two other nuts!
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 

Sadly I built the comission during a very stressful period of my life and there fore I didn’t write down any notes and on how I approached it colors wise but I think I started with a rather dark grey primer coat. I remember that I misted that with Tamiya gun metal, probably also rubbed it with graphite powder. I added the brown as a enamel wash, not with an airbrush. I wanted it to appear random and more like a filter then a sprayed on coat. I then went over certain spots with more grey to tone it down. Finally (and this is what really made it pop) I added a ”dust wash”. Sand colored enamel diluted in white spirit. I also wanted to add snow but I think the buyer decided not to since he was worried it wouldn’t stay on.

I hope I have not offended you! Just like you guys I’m VERY passonate about this model and I just couldn’t recist to join in on the discussion about the colors! Sadly I took very little pictures of the commission build but here’s some showing the finished model before it got packed up. Oh, BTW, I still have my kit gathering dust in the basement. Someday when the kids move out I just might give it a second shoot! 

In the end of the day you really need the ILM model at your side to get this right, even then it might be wrong if it's indeed been tampered with after ESB. I guess the right way is just to knock it off so it suits personal taste, that's probably what would please (at least me) the most!

EDIT: Oh, Guy! I just notised the baby gym in the background in one of your pics! My oldest son used to have the exact same (do you go for the jungle sounds are the music!) before he had a wrestling match on top of it and completely trashed it. I guess that means that you DO have wife and kids!:lol So, what's the secret? Do you use speed?

[IMAGE: Pdroid1.jpg]

[IMAGE: pdroid2.jpg]

[IMAGE: webbase1.jpg]

Cheers,

Steve.

I do know that it has no metallic paint on it though, I used the same Gun Metal on my first PD but never quite liked the look, when I saw it in Sydney the first thing that sprung to my mind was how un metallic it looked. There is also a Vintage ILM video of it on youtube that both me and Lee agree that it has what we call the Blood red look, its impossible to get this with monotone colours like grey and blacks alone.

Post #815  (forum post #1899109)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Sep 18, 2011 at 5:21 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ha, welcome back to the insane club Steve. Its good to know we're not alone in the colour madness. 

A few things I've noticed, if you look at the PD as tones and not colour's then the pics from Chronicles have nearly exact same tonal changes as the prop does today, the colour just doesn't match, at the same time the colour in the CHron pics doesn't match the on screen look either as the hughes are very blue/green. I have noticed a few tell marks in the Chron pics that do line up with the look of the PD today that couldn't exist if a total re paint has happened. Even if it was a wash or misting it would dilute the weathering and change any tones. Its hard to explain without some time in photoshop to show what i mean but will do it over the next few days.

When I saw the prop in front of me it was poorly lit and lit with Daylight bulbs from above only. It did not look brown in the slightest. but the second I took the pics with flash it was clearly very brown in some way. I tried all manner of exposure and ISO setting to get as close to the eye as I could. There are some part of the body that the brown has a distinct line where it turns more to the base colour, these lines are in the Chron pics also, then again we dont know when the Chron pics where taken. The Blu Ray clearly shows a brown hugh that doesn't show up on the DVD. I've not had a chance to look for scaring marks in the weathering yet but I bet I can find some that match the way it looks now.......The more I delve the more convinced I am that its only been re painted around repairs and not modified in colour.

A lot of ref pics are scans of photos and some have had the wrong white balance set for the type of lighting etc etc so it is hard to use old shots for colour matching. What I've tride to do is make it look the same brown at the same distance with flash but still look a muted gun metal grey with low lighting. I think I've managed it, which in turn has given it quite an Olive green tone in normal lighting which turns to a mud Grey/brown depending on angle etc. 

Hand on heart if you paint a PD and take a close up with flash and it doesn't look Brown then i'd say it has to be the wrong colour or missing a key colour in the mix. I would swear blind it had no brown on it from 3-4 feet away when I saw it. In the right light now my PD doesn't look brown at all either. The closer the light the more brown it gets.

I'm like you though, I really want it to be right and nothing else will do.....but if there are 2 camps re the colour then there has to be doubt on both sides.....I'm not budging though, If I give in then I've wasted about 3% of my waking life :lol

Well it feels like that  much time, a bit like Ripley in Alien 3, when she cant remember a time without having to deal with the Alien...I cant remember a time when I woke up and the PD colour didn't bother me:behave:behave:behave

I am up for stealing the PD if you want to join in, It must be on display somewhere and it cant be that hard, we could switch em out take paint samples then put it up for auction with profiles and have new ones made...wait I could just keep it and re paint it to look like mine:eek

Time to go to bed I think...G

Well OK, first round of Graphite buffing. These are taken without flash, on our pooper of a cam, but already, the model now has that metal sheen, and its become very grey, but its still brown, such a hard thing to pull off.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #853  (forum post #1919832)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Sep 28, 2011 at 3:40 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sounds more technical than it is mate, I've only ever done this twice and the first time was on my first PD and I liked the results. 

Its basically enamel thinners with a small amount of light grey mixed with a light tan/yellow, very thin like the brown/ German grey coat. I then just brush (not air) it all over the head and wipe away the excess, it dries in runs if your not careful and I buff it whilst its drying. Then wipe around in places with just thinners on kitchen roll. With the same mix I trickle it around the edges and kit parts similar to an oil wash. I prefer the look of enamel over oil for this as it dries more like dust and looks less like paint. Its not meant to resemble paint but years of dust thats been brushed off and recollected etc etc etc. I'm sure there is a better way of doing it but as I do still make this all up as I go along I just go with it. I just used basic small pots of Humbrol enamel, the cheap stuff.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #881  (forum post #2398281)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Aug 3, 2012 at 6:41 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Seeing as its in the air, here is a tip for the guys about to take on the resin droids knuckle joints.

This was my first set built, using resin as a solid medium to carry the bolt, so, it should work for all.

I used M3 metric screws, but US 4/40 will also be great, the thread is nice and coarse, so holds the tapped bolt well.

First off, drill your "discs" dead centre, if your off, the joint will work, but may foul here and there, and, just look dead horrible, this is VERY

important.

Drilling your discs, or, how you drill them is a matter of taste. I chose to mark and drill them separately, rather than run a drill through two at a time, this seemed messy, and in consistent, faster yes, but i dont do bodge work.

Once your two discs are drilled, (these discs are to be passed through by the bolt) and are a super snug fit to the bolt, you can drill the third disc, bringing the size down, to allow it to be tapped, by the said bolt.

You now, should have three discs, with a bolt running through dead centre, to allow a slight pinch, dont lock it up hard, use very light pressure, you will only really have to adjust these once, from there, you should be able to re pose these legs over and over, without needing to mess around with the pinch bolt.

You can recess the cap head bolt very easily, to allow the Saturn V joint caps to bond over.

[IMAGE: NiceNProbedroidbuild001-22.jpg]

Two drilled discs, ready for the third disc, to make the pinch joint.

[IMAGE: NiceNProbedroidbuild003-15.jpg]

A completed joint, bare bones, but, i think pretty easy to follow and a transferable tech to the new GK you guys will be building soon.

[IMAGE: NiceNProbedroidbuild004-15.jpg]

Just remember, take your time, triple check your markings before drilling, and USE A DRILL PRESS, i use a mini Proxxon, which is awesome for small work like this, and not OTT in price too.

bests..........lee

Post #885  (forum post #2399110)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Aug 3, 2012 at 1:17 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well you could if you can find them in M3 or 4/40 threads, but you dont need them, remember guys, locking a 4/40 bolt into casting plastic is a solid fit, especially, when these things are NON load bearing, you want non of these arms TIGHT....just a slight pinch, so you can just adjust the position, with a fingertip. Youll never really touch the bolt again once set.

lee

Post #930  (forum post #2433854)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Aug 23, 2012 at 11:08 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Julien, you adding motors/servos to your build?

Here's what I plan to do:

Lasercut a series of acrylic circles and braces for the vac formed pieces to ride on, so they don't bear any weight/deform over time.

Head  - main support along the equator. To this the two servos that control the antennas mount, which extend/retract a brass rod that slides inside the other guide brass tubing. I drew a two part component then quickly realized I need to add one more arm in the chain. I'm no engineer, so this will be the hardest part for me, but it should be pretty straightforward. This entire assembly mounts to the 3" bearing and freely rotates with the help of the third servo which will be mounted inside the "neck" armature that nests into the body armature. 

Body top is a lid that bears no weight, and sits on top of the lower body which has three main discs - upper, mid, lower. Upper and mid graft the neck to the body, with the mid being the strongest element as it will also act as the main mount point for the legs and a side mount option. Lowest disc will be the bottom armature mount.

Once I draft all this crap up, I can happily cut copies for people. Does this make sense to do?

[IMAGE: IMG.jpg]

Click to expand...

Jason, yeah I'd like to get the new set for the PD, it's formidale but I'm not sure if I would be able to afford it.

Anyway that how I would do for the antenna. (argh cant upload the pic to my photobucket account, I dont know why).

You dont need the 3rd part you added ! Just make a custon lever/cam (I dont know how you call it) for the servo and it'll work like a charm !

I'm not sure if connecting a servo directly to the head is a good idea. The head is pretty heavy and you would need a big servo (5KG or 7KG), the one you put in big R/C aircraft. Maybe it would be better to use a cam here again. Or why not a gearbox from a 1/16 tank (you should have that, maybe from a 1/15 Bandai tank ?). 

Anyway I think that we should do like we do, us R2 builder, a system with a wheel (tighten up with a spring) to be able to remove the head.

Post #941  (forum post #2435077)
Author    : qcfoundry
Date      : Aug 24, 2012 at 3:45 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

just thought of another way for the antenna:

use string and add a bobbin to the servo's arm.  mount the servo hi -- up against the "scalp" of the antenna hole. also mount the servo/bobbin as close as possible to the the antenna hole.  add an artificial weight to the bottom of the antenna and it will always fall to the low position. turn the servo on to reel the string in and pull the antenna up.

this has less math involved.

math can be hard.

i'm rocking this approach.

Post #965  (forum post #2447769)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Aug 31, 2012 at 1:40 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

For the neck, I'm cutting acrylic discs that will work with both the resin and scratch build options. They will need TB-250 and TB-275, and this 3" lazy susan:

3" Lazy Susan Bearing Swivel - Made by Triangle Manfacturing | eBay

All holes will be pre-drilled, and the acrylic will have a trench etched for the tubing to socket/cement into. You'll be able to use Hyperdyne's kit with this, and I'll tailor it to the servo he recommended.

moffeaton said:

			Any one that got the AT-ST armature was supposed to get all the ref. I provided the reference during that first wave, other people took the torch and ran. So if pics fell through the cracks, I can happily provide them. Gathering them up for a few of you now.
		

Click to expand...

I suspect most people who got all the ref simply don't realize they already have a cropped version of the pic in question that only shows the AT-ST.  As far as I know, the builders of the first wave of replica AT-STs where most part IDs were made (Isel's, Lee's, and mine) didn't have the entire pic in question (with the PD and RT).  In any event, that particular pic of the AT-ST isn't terribly useful, regardless.  I didn't receive the entire uncropped pic until some time after I had completed my AT-ST (and begun work on an RT pattern).  That pic isn't particularly useful for an RT, either.  Don't get me wrong, it's a great pic and I love looking at the old stuff. But, hey, let's keep some perspective, too...

Post #1019  (forum post #2561628)
Author    : joewhite
Date      : Nov 1, 2012 at 10:40 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Just thought I'd throw in a donor tip regarding the leg part from the M18 Howitzer. So, it looks like Esci themselves packaged the M18 in three different variations that I know of so far...not including re-pops by different companies.

German Half-Track M18 Howitzer

7.5 CM Light Infantry Gun #5011

German Artillery Unit w/ W/M-18 Light Howitzer (under Ertl/Esci packaging) #8573

According to my research of all the informative threads, all you need is the M18 part for the leg. If so, the later two kits are better alternatives than the Half-Track/M18 combo. Please correct me if I am wrong about not needing any half-track parts. Just thought I'd throw that out there.

Joe

Post #1027  (forum post #2653896)
Author    : ralphee
Date      : Dec 22, 2012 at 7:43 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

After yet more tweaking of the paint job on this model (another misting of neutral grey), i thought id play around with using Microballoons for the snow/dust effect.

Why i didnt use them sooner i dont know, its no secret its what ILM used, and i wasted so much time with that Delux materials junk.

Microballoons are just awesome for the job, especially, seeing as i just wanted that lightly dusted look as per the Chronicles filming shots.

Just a tip guys, use a good scatter grip glue, and Microballoons, the effect is rather satisfying and scale.

lee

Post #1029  (forum post #2653997)
Author    : qcfoundry
Date      : Dec 22, 2012 at 9:31 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: microballoons.

Are you only dusting the PD, or providing a snowy base? If base,  I recommend making snow clots (like a mud clot). Add water down elementary glue and make a slurry with the MB and let a pile cure on a flat surface. When dry, break pieces off (it's kind of between chalky gypsum and a snow cone). Creates nice chunks. Practice some trial runs - takes a few times to figure the right consistence.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #1033  (forum post #2654595)
Author    : qcfoundry
Date      : Dec 22, 2012 at 6:11 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hate to sound like I'm pimping microballoons, but it's great stuff. You were talking about drifts -- if you give the surface of (dry) MB a soft waft of a breeze, you'll witness it performs exactly like dry snow -- like when a light snow is blowing softly across a bare street and you get these sinuous snakey lines of snow. Would love to freezeframe that with some kind of adhesive. Beautiful looking stuff.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
